class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Developed country</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Developed_country">reviewed</a> on <i>1 October 2018</i>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Industrial nation" redirects here. For the magazine, see <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">Industrialisation</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the investing classification, see <a href="/wiki/Developed_market" title="Developed market">Developed market</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:430px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/428px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png" width="428" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/642px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/856px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2436" data-file-height="1095" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map representing  <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> categories (based on 2017 data, published in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2018_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2018-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="width:100%; background:none;">  <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00023a; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;1.000\xe2\x80\x930.800 (very high)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000074; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.700\xe2\x80\x930.799 (high)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0010c0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.555\xe2\x80\x930.699 (medium)</div> </td> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aabdef; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.350\xe2\x80\x930.554 (low)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a0a0a0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Data unavailable</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>\n<p>A <b>developed  country</b>, <b>industrialized country</b>, <b>more developed country</b>, or <b>more economically developed country</b> (<b>MEDC</b>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> that has a developed economy and advanced technological infrastructure relative to other less industrialized nations. Most commonly, the criteria for evaluating the degree of economic development are <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP), <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">gross national product</a> (GNP), the <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a>, level of industrialization, amount of widespread infrastructure and general standard of living.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Which criteria are to be used and which countries can be classified as being developed are subjects of debate.\n</p><p>Developed countries have generally <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial</a> economies, meaning the <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> provides more wealth than the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial sector">industrial sector</a>. They are contrasted with <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>, which are in the process of <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> or pre-industrial and almost entirely <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agrarian</a>, some of which might fall into the category of <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed country">least developed countries</a>. As of 2015, advanced economies comprise 60.8% of global GDP based on <a href="/wiki/Nominal_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal value">nominal values</a> and 42.9% of global GDP based on <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing-power parity</a> (PPP) according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the ten largest advanced economies by GDP in both nominal and PPP terms were <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Similar_terms"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Similar terms</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Definition_and_criteria"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Definition and criteria</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Human_Development_Index_(HDI)"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Human Development Index (HDI)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#High-income_economies"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">High-income economies</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#World_Bank_high-income_economies"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">World Bank high-income economies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Development_Assistance_Committee_members"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Development Assistance Committee members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#IMF_advanced_economies"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">IMF advanced economies</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Paris_Club_members"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Paris Club members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Similar_terms">Similar terms</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_divide" title="North\xe2\x80\x93South divide">North\xe2\x80\x93South divide</a></div>\n<p>Terms linked to the concept <i>developed country</i> include "advanced country", "industrialized country", "\'more developed country" (MDC), "more economically developed country" (MEDC), "<a href="/wiki/Global_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Global North">Global North</a> country", "<a href="/wiki/First_World" title="First World">first world</a> country", and "post-industrial country". The term industrialized country may be somewhat ambiguous, as <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> is an ongoing process that is hard to define.  The first industrialized country was the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, followed by Belgium. Later it spread further to <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western European</a> countries. According to some <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">economists</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sachs" title="Jeffrey Sachs">Jeffrey Sachs</a>, however, the current divide between the developed and <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing world</a> is largely a phenomenon of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-The_End_of_Poverty_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_End_of_Poverty-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_criteria">Definition and criteria</span></h2>\n<p>Economic criteria have tended to dominate discussions. One such criterion is income per capita; countries with high <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) per capita would thus be described as developed countries.  Another economic criterion is <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>; countries in which the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertiary sector of industry">tertiary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaternary sector of industry">quaternary sectors of industry</a> dominate would thus be described as developed. More recently another measure, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), which combines an economic measure, national income, with other measures, indices for life expectancy and education has become prominent. This criterion would define developed countries as those with a very high (HDI) rating.  The index, however, does not take into account several factors, such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult" title="List of countries by wealth per adult">net wealth per capita</a> or the relative <a href="/wiki/Quality_(business)" title="Quality (business)">quality of goods</a> in a country. This situation tends to lower the ranking for some of the most advanced countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> members and others.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>There is no established convention for the designation of "developed" and "developing" countries or areas in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-unstated.un.org_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstated.un.org-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>And it notes that:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>The designations "developed" and "developing" are intended for statistical convenience and do not necessarily express a judgement about the stage reached by a particular country or area in the development process.<sup id="cite_ref-unstats.un.org_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstats.un.org-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<h2><span id="Human_Development_Index_.28HDI.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Development_Index_(HDI)">Human Development Index (HDI)</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>\n<p>The UN HDI is a statistical measure that gauges a country\'s level of human development. While there is a strong correlation between having a high HDI score and a prosperous economy, the UN points out that the HDI accounts for more than income or productivity. Unlike GDP per capita or per capita income, the HDI takes into account how income is turned "into education and health opportunities and therefore into higher levels of human development."\n</p><p>Since 1990, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932006, 2009\xe2\x80\x932017), <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (1990\xe2\x80\x931991 and 1993), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (1992 and 1994\xe2\x80\x932000) and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (2007\xe2\x80\x932008) have had the highest HDI score.\n</p><p>Many countries listed by IMF or<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> CIA as "advanced", possess an HDI over 0.800, the threshold for "very high" human development. Many countries<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;Note 2&#93;</a></sup> possessing an HDI of 0.800 and over are also listed by IMF or CIA as "advanced". Thus, many "advanced economies" are characterized by an HDI score of 0.800 or higher. Since April 2016, the IMF classifies Macau as an advanced economy.<sup id="cite_ref-qq_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qq-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2018 Human Development Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> was released on 14 September 2018, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2017.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" 0.003\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>As a non-UN member, the government of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> calculates its own HDI, which had a value of 0.882 in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, while the HDI for the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_region" title="Special administrative region">special administrative region</a> of Hong Kong is calculated by the UN, it is not for <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>. The Macanese government calculated the territory\'s HDI to be 0.868 in 2011. These values place both Taiwan and Macau well within the list of countries with "Very high human development".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, in 2009 a United Nations project calculated the HDI for all of its members, as well as Taiwan, Macau, and many <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependent territories</a>. The HDI values for the countries of <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, which have not been included in official annual HDI reports, were found to be at 0.961 and 0.956 respectively. This places both countries firmly within the category of countries with "Very high human development" as well. The dependent territories with HDI values equivalent to "Very high human development" were: <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Escap_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Escap-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Of note, the HDI values in the 2009 report were calculated using the old HDI formula, while HDI values after the year 2010 are calculated with a different formula.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="High-income_economies">High-income economies</span></h2>\n<p>Some institutions have produced lists of developed countries: the UN (list shown above), the CIA,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and some providers of stock market indices (the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_Group" title="FTSE Group">FTSE Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/MSCI" title="MSCI">MSCI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">S&amp;P</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Dow Jones">Dow Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/STOXX" title="STOXX">STOXX</a>, etc.). The latter is not included here because its association of developed countries with countries with both high incomes and <a href="/wiki/Developed_market" title="Developed market">developed markets</a> is not deemed as directly relevant.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title=" (May 2015)">why?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;Note 3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However many other institutions have created more general lists referred to when discussing developed countries. For example, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) identifies 39 "advanced economies".<sup id="cite_ref-qq_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qq-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sanmarino_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanmarino-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>\'s 36 members are known as the "developed countries club"<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> identifies 81 "high income countries".<sup id="cite_ref-wb_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Bank_high-income_economies">World Bank high-income economies</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">World Bank high-income economy</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(nominal,_Atlas_method)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (nominal, Atlas method) per capita">List of countries by GNI (nominal, Atlas method) per capita</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the World Bank the following 81 countries (including territories) are classified as "high-income economies".<sup id="cite_ref-wb_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018, High-income economies are those that had a GNI per capita of $12,056 or more - in 2017.\n</p><p>37 countries and territories wholly or partly members</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:432px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Paris_Club.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/430px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png" width="430" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/645px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/860px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png 2x" data-file-width="1427" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Paris_Club.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are 22 permanent members in the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Club de Paris</i>), a group of officials from major creditor countries whose role is to find coordinated and sustainable solutions to the payment difficulties experienced by debtor countries.\n</p><p>15 countries wholly or partly in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; World</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult" title="List of countries by wealth per adult">List of countries by wealth per adult</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The official classification of "advanced economies" is originally made by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF). The IMF list doesn\'t deal with non-IMF members. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA) intends to follow IMF list but adds few economies which aren\'t dealt with by IMF due to their not being IMF members. By May 2001, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">the advanced country list of the CIA</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080409033504/https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">Archived</a> 9 April 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. was more comprehensive than the original IMF list. However, since May 2001, three additional countries (<a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>) have been added to the original IMF list, thus leaving the CIA list not updated.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Namely sovereign states, i.e., excluding <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>: In 2003, the government of Macau calculated its HDI as being 0.909 (the UN does not calculate Macau\'s HDI); In January 2007, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://english.people.com.cn/200701/29/eng20070129_345749.html">People\'s Daily</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081207054232/http://english.people.com.cn/200701/29/eng20070129_345749.html">Archived</a> 7 December 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. reported (from <i>China Modernization Report 2007</i>): "In 2004... Macau... had reached the level of developed countries". The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.unctad.org/en/docs/tdstat30_enfr.pdf">UNCTAD</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070710000327/http://www.unctad.org/en/docs/tdstat30_enfr.pdf">Archived</a> 10 July 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. organisation (of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>), as well as the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">CIA</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080409033504/https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">Archived</a> 9 April 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>., classify Macau as a "developing" territory. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.worldbank.org/servlets/ECR?contentMDK=20421402&amp;sitePK=239419#High_income">World Bank</a> classifies Macau as a high income economy (along with developed economies as well as with few developing economies).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ftse.com/products/downloads/FTSE-Country-Classification-Update_latest.pdf">The Developed Countries Glossary</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141220104324/http://www.ftse.com/products/downloads/FTSE-Country-Classification-Update_latest.pdf">Archived</a> 20 December 2014 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. entry reads: "The following countries are classified by FTSE as developed countries: Australia, Austria, Belgium/Luxembourg, Canada, Denmark, Finland, France, Germany, Greece, Hong Kong (People\'s Republic of China), Ireland, Israel, Italy, Japan, Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Portugal, Singapore, South Korea, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland, United Kingdom and the United States."</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
